This place is one of the things I miss most about California..I lived there for 8 years, the last 4 in Marin. I would walk to the coffee shop, right in the heart of town, from my kids home in San Anselmo ( I babysat when my first grand baby was born ). I recommected with a childhood friend (I grew up in Michigan) whose daughter moved there, just blocks from my kids...small world. We hadn‚Äôt seen each other in 40 years!  I‚Äôd get my coffee and sit on one of the benches to enjoy in Imagination park and often see George Lucas stroll by. This was the place for me. Live music on the weekends. My little grandson really loved it. Oh, how I miss this place. By the way, the best coffee drinks (my fav, turmeric lattes) ever constructed...üå∫üíï Great food, great atmosphere, lots of regulars...simply the best.‚ù§Ô∏è<//review>

<name>Lisa Ma</name><Time>1393141784980<//Time><Rating>5< /Rating>< text>
The Fremont Thai Temple is a peaceful place to enjoy an authentic Thai brunch, while supporting a great cause.  There are many food stalls to choose from as well as picnic tables in the surrounding gardens.  First, trade in your dollars for tokens to buy food at the stalls.

My favorites are:

+ Shrimp Pad Thai: Best pad thai ever!  Fresh and made to order so put your name on the list as soon as you arrive
+ Thai Noodle Soup: Fresh, spicy and comforting
+ Sticky Rice Dumpling Stuffed with Spinach: Very tasty
+ Mango Sticky Rice: Very authentic
+ Black Sticky Rice with Egg Custard: Sweet and delicious

Tip: Hiking trails nearby at Coyote Hills or further at Mission Peak...to work off the food.</text>

< Text>
How cool that even with most pumpkin patches closed, we still were able to visit here in Bonita. It was the simple things that made it fun. The corn maze, the hay ride, and the goats. We did social distancing and everyone had to wear a mask, so that was good. This pumpkin patch is good for all ages. There is also plenty of parking. I came at daytime and also at night.  You can only do hay ride and corn maze during the day so keep that in mind when planning your visit.<//Text>

<Resp>None<//Resp>< text>
This is the first pumpkin patch we have ever been to and we really enjoyed it! We went this weekend and it was so busy. The main parking lot can get full fast; there is overflow parking at the church if you need it. Everyone wore masks and kept their distance. The admission is free, which is awesome especially if you are on a budget! There are lots of pretty photo-ops everywhere. Other things to do are the hayride, train station, corn maze, and the petting zoo. I think the attractions range from $2 per person, $4 per kid with 1 free adult for the petting zoo--an extra dollar to feed the goats. You can also pick/buy your own pumpkins and sunflowers.< /text>
